# Airborne Networking

## Challenges

### Current Technology Restrictions

Many challenges lie ahead before the AN will exist as described in this document. Many of the challenges currently lie in the Legacy system avionics found on all aircraft. The biggest obstacle is a lack in bandwidth. Until more optics are integrated into aircraft systems, this system will lag in data transfer speeds and latency. One technology under research to resolve this problem is the Navy's research into highly integrated photonics to manage aircraft sensor suite communications. The technique runs radio frequencies over fiber optics and is currently being integrated into the EA-6B Prowler electronic warfare jet.

Security of this network is another huge obstacle. The goal is to give the system a low probability of jamming and interception. Many ideas of how to protect the system are being investigated and tested. Traditional methods of authentication and authorization are being used, to include biometrics, cryptographic tokens, and integrated Public Key Infrastructure.

### Commercial Off-the-Shelf

Commercial off-the-shelf (COTS) creates extreme engineering challenges. While it offers flexibility in application and saves money in production it is incredibly difficult to adapt to various application. Getting COTS to install in applications it was not designed for continues to be a vast engineering challenge as military researchers work to integrate civilian L-3 radio and FPGA technology into reconnaissance aircraft designed in the 60s.

### Bandwidth

Bandwidth to support the Air Force's AN does not currently exist. Only time can tell until enough bandwidth is freed up by obsolete technology. This creates the challenge of creating better ways of compressing data and developing more efficient ways to utilize the bandwidth currently available. One interim solution developed by Northrop Grumman is the Dialup rate IP over existing radios (DRIER). DRIER enables airborne or ground-based tactic

#### Six Sigma in Aerospace

Six Sigma is a data-driven methodology that has been widely adopted in various industries, including aerospace. It focuses on reducing defects and improving process efficiency, making it crucial in the highly regulated and safety-conscious field of aerospace. In this section, we will explore the unique challenges and benefits of applying Six Sigma in the aerospace industry.

##### Unique Challenges in Aerospace

The aerospace industry faces several unique challenges that make the application of Six Sigma methods essential. One of the main challenges is the high level of safety and precision required in the production and maintenance of aircraft. Even the smallest errors can have catastrophic consequences, making it crucial to have efficient processes in place to ensure the highest level of quality and safety.

In addition, the aerospace industry has a complex supply chain and high costs of materials and production. This further emphasizes the need for efficient processes to reduce waste and improve overall productivity. The long development cycles and high level of precision required in aerospace engineering also make it essential to have processes that are not only efficient but also highly accurate and reliable.

##### Tools and Techniques Used in Six Sigma

Six Sigma utilizes a variety of tools and techniques to identify and eliminate defects and improve processes. These include statistical process control, root cause analysis, and design of experiments. In the aerospace industry, these tools can be applied to address specific challenges and improve processes.

Statistical process control (SPC) is a method used to monitor and control a process by analyzing data and identifying any variations or abnormalities. In the aerospace industry, SPC can be used to monitor critical processes and identify any potential issues before they lead to defects or safety concerns.

Root cause analysis is another important tool in Six Sigma, which helps identify the underlying causes of defects or issues in a process. This is crucial in the aerospace industry, where even small errors can have significant consequences. By identifying the root cause, steps can be taken to prevent similar issues from occurring in the future.

Design of experiments (DOE) is a statistical method used to systematically test and analyze different variables in a process to determine the most efficient and effective combination. In the aerospace industry, DOE can be used to optimize processes and improve overall efficiency.

### Section: 20.4 Challenges in Aerospace

The aerospace industry presents unique challenges for process improvement, making it an ideal application for Lean Six Sigma methods. These challenges include technology restrictions, commercial off-the-shelf (COTS) integration, and limited bandwidth.

#### Technology Restrictions

One of the main challenges in the aerospace industry is the use of legacy systems and outdated technology. This can lead to limitations in data transfer speeds and latency, hindering the efficiency of processes. To overcome this challenge, the industry is constantly researching and implementing new technologies, such as highly integrated photonics, to improve data transfer speeds and overall performance.

#### Commercial Off-the-Shelf (COTS) Integration

The use of commercial off-the-shelf (COTS) components in aerospace systems presents a significant engineering challenge. While COTS components offer flexibility and cost savings, they are not always designed for the specific applications in the aerospace industry. This creates the need for extensive adaptation and integration efforts, which can be time-consuming and costly.

#### Limited Bandwidth

Bandwidth is a critical factor in the aerospace industry, as it affects the speed and efficiency of data transfer. However, the current bandwidth available is limited, and it is not always possible to increase it due to obsolete technology. To address this challenge, companies are developing innovative solutions, such as the Dialup rate IP over existing radios (DRIER), to make the most of the available bandwidth and improve data transfer efficiency.

### Subsection: 20.4.1 Security Challenges

In addition to the technical challenges, security is also a major concern in the aerospace industry. With the increasing use of technology and data transfer, the risk of cyber attacks and data breaches is a significant threat. To ensure the safety and security of aerospace systems, companies are implementing traditional methods of authentication and authorization, as well as exploring new technologies such as biometrics and cryptographic tokens. The goal is to create a low probability of jamming and interception, ensuring the integrity and confidentiality of sensitive data.

Overall, the aerospace industry presents unique challenges for process improvement, making it an ideal application for Lean Six Sigma methods. By addressing these challenges and utilizing tools and techniques such as statistical process control, root cause analysis, and design of experiments, companies can improve efficiency, reduce waste, and ensure the highest level of quality and safety in their processes.
